      <p><b>Tonga</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/ɒ/: 'o' in 'body'">ɒ</span><span title="/ŋ/: 'ng' in 'sing'">ŋ</span></span>(<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ɡ/: 'g' in 'guy'">ɡ</span></span>)<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <a href="/wiki/Tongan_language" title="Tongan language">Tongan</a>: <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[ˈtoŋa]</a></span><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> <i>Puleʻanga Fakatuʻi ʻo Tonga</i>), officially named the <b>Kingdom of Tonga</b>, is a <a href="/wiki/Polynesia" title="Polynesia">Polynesian</a> country and <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">archipelago</a> comprising <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_and_towns_in_Tonga" title="List of islands and towns in Tonga">169 islands</a>, of which 36 are inhabited.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup> The archipelago’s total surface area is about 750 square kilometres (290&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) scattered over 700,000 square kilometres (270,000&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) of the southern <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a>. As of 2016, Tonga had a population of 100,651 inhabitants,<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2019_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP_2019-10">[10]</a></sup> of whom 70% reside on the main island, <a href="/wiki/Tongatapu" title="Tongatapu">Tongatapu</a>. </p>
      <p>Tonga stretches across approximately 800 kilometres (500&nbsp;mi) in a north–south line. It is surrounded by <a href="/wiki/Fiji" title="Fiji">Fiji</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wallis_and_Futuna" title="Wallis and Futuna">Wallis and Futuna</a> (<a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>) to the northwest; <a href="/wiki/Samoa" title="Samoa">Samoa</a> to the northeast; <a href="/wiki/New_Caledonia" title="New Caledonia">New Caledonia</a> (France) and <a href="/wiki/Vanuatu" title="Vanuatu">Vanuatu</a> to the west; <a href="/wiki/Niue" title="Niue">Niue</a> (the nearest foreign territory) to the east; and <a href="/wiki/Kermadec_Islands" title="Kermadec Islands">Kermadec</a> to the southwest. (Niue and Kermadec are both part of <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>). Tonga is about 1,800 kilometres (1,100&nbsp;mi) from New Zealand's <a href="/wiki/North_Island" title="North Island">North Island</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Tonga_(1900%E2%80%931970)" title="Kingdom of Tonga (1900–1970)">From 1900 to 1970, Tonga had British protected-state status</a>. The <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> looked after its foreign affairs under a <a href="#History">Treaty of Friendship</a>. But Tonga never relinquished its <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">sovereignty</a> to any foreign power.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> In 2010, Tonga took a decisive step away from its traditional absolute monarchy and towards becoming a fully functioning <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a>, after <a href="/wiki/Legislature" title="Legislature">legislative</a> reforms paved the way for its first partial <a href="/wiki/Representative_election" class="mw-redirect" title="Representative election">representative elections</a>. </p> 
      <div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading">

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tonga&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>In many <a href="/wiki/Polynesian_languages" title="Polynesian languages">Polynesian languages</a>, including Tongan, the word <i>tonga</i> comes from <i>fakatonga</i>, which means "southwards", and the archipelago is so named because it is the southernmost group among the islands of central <a href="/wiki/Polynesia" title="Polynesia">Polynesia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> The word <i>tonga</i> is cognate to the <a href="/wiki/Hawai%CA%BBi_(island)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hawaiʻi (island)">Hawaiian</a> word “kona,” meaning “leeward,” which is the origin of the name for the <a href="/wiki/Kona_District,_Hawai%CA%BBi" class="mw-redirect" title="Kona District, Hawaiʻi">Kona District in Hawai’i</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Tonga became known in the West as the "Friendly Islands" because of the congenial reception accorded to <a href="/wiki/James_Cook" title="James Cook">Captain James Cook</a> on his first visit in 1773. He arrived at the time of the annual <i>ʻinasi</i> festival, which centers on the donation of the <a href="/wiki/First_Fruits" title="First Fruits">First Fruits</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Tu%CA%BBi_Tonga" title="Tuʻi Tonga">Tuʻi Tonga</a> (the islands' paramount chief), and so he received an invitation to the festivities. Ironically, according to the writer <a href="/wiki/William_Mariner_(writer)" title="William Mariner (writer)">William Mariner</a>, the chiefs actually wanted to kill Cook during the gathering, but didn’t go through with it because they couldn’t agree on a plan of action for accomplishing it.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tonga&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Tonga" title="History of Tonga">History of Tonga</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tasman-dagboek-a.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Tasman-dagboek-a.jpg/220px-Tasman-dagboek-a.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Tasman-dagboek-a.jpg/330px-Tasman-dagboek-a.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Tasman-dagboek-a.jpg/440px-Tasman-dagboek-a.jpg 2x" data-file-width="988" data-file-height="631"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tasman-dagboek-a.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The arrival of <a href="/wiki/Abel_Tasman" title="Abel Tasman">Abel Tasman</a> in Tongatapu, 1643; drawing by <a href="/wiki/Isaack_Gilsemans" title="Isaack Gilsemans">Isaack Gilsemans</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:NL-HaNA_1.11.01.01_121_0051_Scheepsjournaal_Abel_Tasman_35.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/NL-HaNA_1.11.01.01_121_0051_Scheepsjournaal_Abel_Tasman_35.jpg/220px-NL-HaNA_1.11.01.01_121_0051_Scheepsjournaal_Abel_Tasman_35.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="335" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/NL-HaNA_1.11.01.01_121_0051_Scheepsjournaal_Abel_Tasman_35.jpg/330px-NL-HaNA_1.11.01.01_121_0051_Scheepsjournaal_Abel_Tasman_35.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/NL-HaNA_1.11.01.01_121_0051_Scheepsjournaal_Abel_Tasman_35.jpg/440px-NL-HaNA_1.11.01.01_121_0051_Scheepsjournaal_Abel_Tasman_35.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1973" data-file-height="3000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:NL-HaNA_1.11.01.01_121_0051_Scheepsjournaal_Abel_Tasman_35.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Page from the ship's log of Abel Tasman with the description of t' Eijlandt Amsterdam, nowadays Tongatapu<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>An <a href="/wiki/Austronesian_languages" title="Austronesian languages">Austronesian</a>-speaking group linked to what archaeologists call the <a href="/wiki/Lapita_culture" title="Lapita culture">Lapita</a> cultural complex reached and inhabited Tonga sometime between 1500 and 1000&nbsp;BC.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> Scholars still debate exactly when Tonga was first settled, but <a href="/wiki/Thorium" title="Thorium">thorium</a> dating confirms that settlers had arrived in the earliest known inhabited town, Nukuleka, by 888 BC, ± 8 years.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> Not much is known for sure about Tonga’s history before European contact, because Tongans lacked a <a href="/wiki/Writing_system" title="Writing system">writing system</a>, but they did have an <a href="/wiki/Oral_history" title="Oral history">oral history</a>, which had been passed down and was set down in writing after the arrival of the Europeans. </p>
      <p>By the 12th century, Tongans and the Tongan paramount chief, the <a href="/wiki/Tu%CA%BBi_Tonga" title="Tuʻi Tonga">Tuʻi Tonga</a>, had acquired a reputation across the central Pacific—from <a href="/wiki/Niue" title="Niue">Niue</a>, <a href="/wiki/Samoa" title="Samoa">Samoa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rotuma" title="Rotuma">Rotuma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wallis_%26_Futuna" class="mw-redirect" title="Wallis &amp; Futuna">Wallis &amp; Futuna</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Caledonia" title="New Caledonia">New Caledonia</a> to <a href="/wiki/Tikopia" title="Tikopia">Tikopia</a>—leading some historians to speak of there having been a <a href="/wiki/Tu%CA%BBi_Tonga_Empire" title="Tuʻi Tonga Empire">Tuʻi Tonga Empire</a> during that period. There are also known to have been civil wars in Tonga in the 15th and 17th centuries. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:William_Mariner_(1791-1853)_crop.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/William_Mariner_%281791-1853%29_crop.jpg/200px-William_Mariner_%281791-1853%29_crop.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="433" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/6e/William_Mariner_%281791-1853%29_crop.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="270" data-file-height="585"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:William_Mariner_(1791-1853)_crop.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/William_Mariner_(writer)" title="William Mariner (writer)">William Mariner</a> was a teenage English sailor adopted into a royal Tongan family.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Tongan people first encountered Europeans in 1616, when the Dutch vessel <a href="/wiki/Eendracht_(1615_ship)" class="mw-redirect" title="Eendracht (1615 ship)"><i>Eendracht</i></a>, captained by <a href="/wiki/Willem_Schouten" title="Willem Schouten">Willem Schouten</a>, made a short visit to the islands for the purpose of engaging in trade. Later, other Dutch explorers arrived, including <a href="/wiki/Jacob_Le_Maire" title="Jacob Le Maire">Jacob Le Maire</a> (who visited the northern island of <a href="/wiki/Niuatoputapu" title="Niuatoputapu">Niuatoputapu</a>); and <a href="/wiki/Abel_Tasman" title="Abel Tasman">Abel Tasman</a> (who visited <a href="/wiki/Tongatapu" title="Tongatapu">Tongatapu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ha%CA%BBapai" title="Haʻapai">Haʻapai</a>) in 1643. Later noteworthy European visitors included <a href="/wiki/James_Cook" title="James Cook">James Cook</a>, of the British Royal Navy, in 1773, 1774, and 1777; Spanish Navy explorers <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Mourelle" class="mw-redirect" title="Francisco Mourelle">Francisco Mourelle de la Rúa</a> in 1781; <a href="/wiki/Alessandro_Malaspina" class="mw-redirect" title="Alessandro Malaspina">Alessandro Malaspina</a> in 1793; the first London <a href="/wiki/Missionaries" class="mw-redirect" title="Missionaries">missionaries</a> in 1797; and the <a href="/wiki/Methodism" title="Methodism">Wesleyan Methodist</a> minister, Reverend Walter Lawry, in 1822. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Whaling" title="Whaling">Whaling</a> vessels were among the earliest regular Western visitors. The first of these on record is the <i>Ann &amp; Hope</i>, which was reported to have been seen among the islands of Tonga in June 1799.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> The last known whaling visitor was the <i>Albatross</i> in 1899. That ship arrived in Tonga seeking a re-supply of water, food and wood. The islands most regularly visited by Westerners were Ata, 'Eua, Ha'apai, Tongatapu and Vava'u. Sometimes Tongan men were recruited to serve as crewmen on these vessels. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Exploring_Expedition" title="United States Exploring Expedition">United States Exploring Expedition</a> visited Tonga in 1840.<sup id="cite_ref-Stanton_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stanton-19">[19]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1845, an ambitious young Tongan warrior, strategist, and orator named <a href="/wiki/T%C4%81ufa%CA%BB%C4%81hau" class="mw-redirect" title="Tāufaʻāhau">Tāufaʻāhau</a> united Tonga into a kingdom. He held the chiefly title of <a href="/wiki/Tu%CA%BBi_Kanokupolu" title="Tuʻi Kanokupolu">Tuʻi Kanokupolu</a>, but had been baptised by <a href="/wiki/Methodist" class="mw-redirect" title="Methodist">Methodist</a> missionaries with the name <i>Siaosi</i> ("George") in 1831. In 1875, with the help of missionary <a href="/wiki/Shirley_Waldemar_Baker" title="Shirley Waldemar Baker">Shirley Waldemar Baker</a>, he declared Tonga a constitutional monarchy; formally adopted the Western royal style; emancipated the "serfs"; enshrined a code of law, land tenure, and freedom of the press; and limited the power of the chiefs. </p>
      <p>Tonga became a <a href="/wiki/British_Protectorate" class="mw-redirect" title="British Protectorate">protected state</a> under a <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Friendship" title="Treaty of Friendship">Treaty of Friendship</a> with Britain on 18 May 1900, when European settlers and rival Tongan chiefs unsuccessfully tried to oust the man who had succeeded Tāufaʻāhau as king. The treaty posted no higher permanent representative on Tonga than a British <a href="/wiki/Consul_(representative)" title="Consul (representative)">Consul</a> (1901–1970). Under the protection of Britain, Tonga maintained its sovereignty, and remained the only Pacific nation to retain its monarchical government. The Tongan monarchy follows an uninterrupted succession of hereditary rulers from one family.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/1918_flu_pandemic" class="mw-redirect" title="1918 flu pandemic">1918 flu pandemic</a>, brought to Tonga by a ship from New Zealand, killed 1,800 Tongans: a mortality rate of about eight percent.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Treaty of Friendship and Tonga's protection status ended in 1970 under arrangements that had been established by Tonga’s Queen <a href="/wiki/Salote_Tupou_III" class="mw-redirect" title="Salote Tupou III">Salote Tupou III</a> before her death in 1965. Owing to its British ties, Tonga joined the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth</a> in 1970 (atypically as a country that had its own monarch, rather than being ruled by the United Kingdom’s monarch), along with <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lesotho" title="Lesotho">Lesotho</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Eswatini" title="Eswatini">Eswatini</a> (Swaziland). Tonga became a member of the United Nations in September 1999. While exposed to colonial pressures, Tonga has always governed itself, which makes it unique in the Pacific. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tonga&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Tonga" title="Politics of Tonga">Politics of Tonga</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:King_George,_of_the_Friendly_Islands_(1852,_p.1,_IX)_-_Copy.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/King_George%2C_of_the_Friendly_Islands_%281852%2C_p.1%2C_IX%29_-_Copy.jpg/220px-King_George%2C_of_the_Friendly_Islands_%281852%2C_p.1%2C_IX%29_-_Copy.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="168" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/King_George%2C_of_the_Friendly_Islands_%281852%2C_p.1%2C_IX%29_-_Copy.jpg/330px-King_George%2C_of_the_Friendly_Islands_%281852%2C_p.1%2C_IX%29_-_Copy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/King_George%2C_of_the_Friendly_Islands_%281852%2C_p.1%2C_IX%29_-_Copy.jpg/440px-King_George%2C_of_the_Friendly_Islands_%281852%2C_p.1%2C_IX%29_-_Copy.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1267" data-file-height="965"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:King_George,_of_the_Friendly_Islands_(1852,_p.1,_IX)_-_Copy.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>King George, of the Friendly Islands (1852)<sup id="cite_ref-Juvenile1852_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Juvenile1852-22">[22]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Tonga is a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a>. It is the only indigenous monarchy in the Pacific islands. Reverence for the monarch replaces that held in earlier centuries for the sacred paramount chief, the Tuʻi Tonga. Criticism of the monarch is held to be contrary to Tongan culture and etiquette. King <a href="/wiki/Tupou_VI" title="Tupou VI">Tupou VI</a> (a descendant of the first monarch), his family, powerful nobles and a growing non-royal elite caste live in much wealth, with the rest of the country living in relative poverty. </p>
      <p>Tonga provides for its citizens a free and mandatory education for all, secondary education with only nominal fees, and foreign-funded scholarships for post-secondary education. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:George_Tupou_I,_c._1880s.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/George_Tupou_I%2C_c._1880s.jpg/220px-George_Tupou_I%2C_c._1880s.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="282" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/George_Tupou_I%2C_c._1880s.jpg/330px-George_Tupou_I%2C_c._1880s.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/George_Tupou_I%2C_c._1880s.jpg/440px-George_Tupou_I%2C_c._1880s.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1036" data-file-height="1328"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:George_Tupou_I,_c._1880s.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/T%C4%81ufa%CA%BB%C4%81hau" class="mw-redirect" title="Tāufaʻāhau">Tāufaʻāhau</a>, King of Tonga (1845–1893)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The pro-democracy movement in Tonga promotes reforms, including better representation in the Parliament for the majority of commoners, and better accountability in matters of state. An overthrow of the monarchy is not part of the movement and the institution of monarchy continues to hold popular support, even while reforms are advocated. Until recently, the governance issue was generally ignored by the leaders of other countries, but major aid donors and neighbours New Zealand and Australia are now expressing concerns about some Tongan government actions. </p>
      <p>Following the precedents of Queen Sālote and the counsel of numerous international advisors,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (February 2010)">who?</span></a></i>]</sup> the government of Tonga under King <a href="/wiki/T%C4%81ufa%CA%BB%C4%81hau_Tupou_IV" title="Tāufaʻāhau Tupou IV">Tāufaʻāhau Tupou IV</a> (reigned 1965–2006) monetised the economy, internationalised the medical and education system, and enabled access by commoners to increasing forms of material wealth (houses, cars, and other commodities), education, and overseas travel. </p>
      <p>Male <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Tonga" title="LGBT rights in Tonga">homosexuality</a> is illegal in Tonga,<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> with a maximum penalty of 10 years' imprisonment.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> Tongans have universal access to a national health care system. The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Tonga" title="Constitution of Tonga">Constitution of Tonga</a> protects land ownership: land cannot be sold to foreigners (although it may be leased).<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_culture">Political culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tonga&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Political culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kingtupou.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Kingtupou.jpg/220px-Kingtupou.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Kingtupou.jpg/330px-Kingtupou.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Kingtupou.jpg/440px-Kingtupou.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1459" data-file-height="1000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kingtupou.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Tupou_VI" title="Tupou VI">King Tupou VI</a> during his coronation on 4 July 2015
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>King Tāufaʻāhau Tupou IV, and his government made some problematic economic decisions and were accused by democracy activists, including former prime minister <a href="/wiki/%CA%BBAkilisi_P%C5%8Dhiva" title="ʻAkilisi Pōhiva">ʻAkilisi Pōhiva</a>, of wasting millions of dollars on unwise investments. The problems have mostly been driven by attempts to increase national revenue through a variety of schemes: considering making Tonga a nuclear waste disposal site (an idea floated in the mid 1990s by the current crown prince);<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> and selling Tongan Protected Persons Passports (which eventually forced Tonga to naturalise the purchasers, sparking ethnicity-based concerns within Tonga).<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Schemes also included the registering of foreign ships (which proved to be engaged in illegal activities, including shipments for <a href="/wiki/Al-Qaeda" title="Al-Qaeda">al-Qaeda</a>);<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> claiming geo-orbital satellite slots (the revenue from which seems to belong to the Princess Royal, not the state);<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> holding a long-term charter on an unusable <a href="/wiki/Boeing_757" title="Boeing 757">Boeing 757</a> that was sidelined in <a href="/wiki/Auckland" title="Auckland">Auckland</a> Airport, leading to the collapse of <a href="/wiki/Royal_Tongan_Airlines" title="Royal Tongan Airlines">Royal Tongan Airlines</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> and approving a factory for exporting cigarettes to China (against the advice of Tongan medical officials, and decades of health promotion messaging).<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The king proved vulnerable to speculators with big promises and lost reportedly US$26&nbsp;million to <a href="/wiki/Jesse_Bogdonoff" title="Jesse Bogdonoff">Jesse Bogdonoff</a>, a financial adviser who called himself the king's <a href="/wiki/Jester" title="Jester">Court Jester</a>. The police imprisoned pro-democracy leaders, and the government repeatedly confiscated the newspaper <i>The Tongan Times</i> (printed in New Zealand and sold in Tonga) because the editor had been vocally critical of the king's mistakes.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> Notably, the <i>Keleʻa</i>, produced specifically to critique the government and printed in Tonga by pro-democracy leader ʻAkilisi Pōhiva, was not banned during that time. Pōhiva, however, had been subjected to harassment in the form of <a href="/wiki/Barratry_(common_law)" title="Barratry (common law)">barratry</a> (frequent lawsuits).<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In mid-2003, the government passed a radical constitutional amendment to "Tonganize" the press, by licensing and limiting freedom of the press, so as to protect the image of the monarchy. The amendment was defended by the government and by royalists on the basis of traditional cultural values. Licensure criteria include 80% ownership by Tongans living in the country. As of February&nbsp;2004<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tonga&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, those papers denied licenses under the new act included the <i>Taimi ʻo Tonga</i> (<i>Tongan Times</i>), the <i>Keleʻa,</i> and the <i>Matangi Tonga</i>—while those permitted licenses were uniformly church-based or pro-government. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Royal_Palace,_Nuku%27alofa.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Royal_Palace%2C_Nuku%27alofa.jpg/220px-Royal_Palace%2C_Nuku%27alofa.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Royal_Palace%2C_Nuku%27alofa.jpg/330px-Royal_Palace%2C_Nuku%27alofa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Royal_Palace%2C_Nuku%27alofa.jpg/440px-Royal_Palace%2C_Nuku%27alofa.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3796" data-file-height="2800"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Royal_Palace,_Nuku%27alofa.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Palace,_Tonga" title="Royal Palace, Tonga">Royal palace of Tonga</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The bill was opposed in the form of a several-thousand-strong protest march in the capital, a call by the Tuʻi Pelehake (a prince, nephew of the king and elected member of parliament) for Australia and other nations to pressure the Tongan government to democratise the electoral system, and a legal writ calling for a judicial investigation of the bill. The latter was supported by some 160 signatures, including seven of the nine elected, "People's Representatives". </p>
      <p>The then Crown Prince <a href="/wiki/George_Tupou_V" title="George Tupou V">Tupoutoʻa</a> and Pilolevu, the Princess Royal, remained generally silent on the issue. In total, the changes threatened to destabilise the polity, fragment support for the status quo, and place further pressure on the monarchy. </p>
      <p>In 2005, the government spent several weeks negotiating with striking civil-service workers before reaching a settlement. The civil unrest that ensued was not limited to Tonga; protests outside the King's New Zealand residence made headlines. </p>
      <p>Prime Minister Prince <a href="/wiki/Tupou_VI" title="Tupou VI">ʻAhoʻeitu ʻUnuakiʻotonga Tukuʻaho (Lavaka Ata ʻUlukālala)</a> (now King Tupou VI) resigned suddenly on 11 February 2006, and also gave up his other cabinet portfolios. The elected Minister of Labour, Dr <a href="/wiki/Feleti_Sevele" title="Feleti Sevele">Feleti Sevele</a>, replaced him in the interim. </p>
      <p>On 5 July 2006, a driver in <a href="/wiki/Menlo_Park,_California" title="Menlo Park, California">Menlo Park, California</a>, caused the deaths of Prince <a href="/wiki/Tu%CA%BBipelehake_(%CA%BBUluvalu)" class="mw-redirect" title="Tuʻipelehake (ʻUluvalu)">Tuʻipelehake ʻUluvalu</a>, his wife, and their driver. Tuʻipelehake, 55, was the co-chairman of the constitutional reform commission, and a nephew of the King. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Looters.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Looters.jpg/220px-Looters.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Looters.jpg/330px-Looters.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Looters.jpg/440px-Looters.jpg 2x" data-file-width="747" data-file-height="576"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Looters.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Riots in Nukuʻalofa, 2006
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The public expected some changes when George Tupou V succeeded his father in September 2006. On <a href="/wiki/2006_Tonga_riots" class="mw-redirect" title="2006 Tonga riots">16 November 2006, rioting broke out</a> in the capital city of <a href="/wiki/Nuku%CA%BBalofa" title="Nukuʻalofa">Nukuʻalofa</a> when it seemed that the parliament would adjourn for the year without having made any advances in increasing democracy in government. Pro-democracy activists burned and looted shops, offices, and government buildings. As a result, more than 60% of the downtown area was destroyed, and as many as 6&nbsp;people died.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> The disturbances were ended by action from <a href="/wiki/His_Majesty%27s_Armed_Forces_(Tonga)" title="His Majesty's Armed Forces (Tonga)">Tongan Security Forces</a> and troops from New Zealand-led Joint Task Force.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 29 July 2008, the Palace announced that King George Tupou V would relinquish much of his power and would surrender his role in day-to-day governmental affairs to the Prime Minister. The royal chamberlain said that this was being done to prepare the monarchy for 2010, when most of the first parliament would be elected, and added: "The Sovereign of the only Polynesian kingdom... is voluntarily surrendering his powers to meet the democratic aspirations of many of his people." The previous week, the government said the king had sold state assets that had contributed so much of the royal family's wealth.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 15 March 2012, King George Tupou V contracted pneumonia and was brought to <a href="/wiki/Queen_Mary_Hospital_(Hong_Kong)" title="Queen Mary Hospital (Hong Kong)">Queen Mary Hospital</a> in <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>. He was later diagnosed with leukaemia. His health deteriorated significantly shortly thereafter, and he died at 3:15&nbsp;pm on 18 March 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> He was succeeded by his brother <a href="/wiki/Tupou_VI" title="Tupou VI">Tupou VI</a>, who was crowned on 4 July 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tonga&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Tonga" title="Foreign relations of Tonga">Foreign relations of Tonga</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Tonga's foreign policy as of January 2009<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tonga&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> has been described by <a href="/wiki/Matangi_Tonga" title="Matangi Tonga">Matangi Tonga</a> as "Look East"—specifically, as establishing closer diplomatic and economic relations with <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a> (which actually lies to the north-west of the Pacific kingdom). Tonga retains cordial relations with the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>. Although it remains on good terms with the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, the two countries do not maintain particularly close relations, and the United Kingdom closed its High Commission in Tonga in 2006, although the UK High Commission was re-established in January 2020 after a 14-year absence. Tonga's relations with Oceania's regional powers, <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, are good.<sup id="cite_ref-matangitonga.to_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-matangitonga.to-39">[39]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Tonga maintains strong regional ties in the Pacific. It is a full member of the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Islands_Forum" title="Pacific Islands Forum">Pacific Islands Forum</a>, the <a href="/wiki/South_Pacific_Applied_Geoscience_Commission" title="South Pacific Applied Geoscience Commission">South Pacific Applied Geoscience Commission</a>, the <a href="/wiki/South_Pacific_Tourism_Organisation" title="South Pacific Tourism Organisation">South Pacific Tourism Organisation</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Regional_Environment_Programme" title="Pacific Regional Environment Programme">Pacific Regional Environment Programme</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Secretariat_of_the_Pacific_Community" class="mw-redirect" title="Secretariat of the Pacific Community">Secretariat of the Pacific Community</a>. </p>
      <p>In March 2017, at the 34th regular session of the UN Human Rights Council, <a href="/wiki/Vanuatu" title="Vanuatu">Vanuatu</a> made a joint statement on behalf of Tonga and some other Pacific nations raising human rights violations in the <a href="/wiki/Western_New_Guinea" title="Western New Guinea">Western New Guinea</a>, which has been occupied by <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> since 1963,<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> and requested that the UN High Commissioner for Human Rights produce a report.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SBSMar17_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SBSMar17-42">[42]</a></sup> Indonesia rejected allegations.<sup id="cite_ref-SBSMar17_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SBSMar17-42">[42]</a></sup> More than 100,000 Papuans have died during a 50-year <a href="/wiki/Papua_conflict" title="Papua conflict">Papua conflict</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tonga&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tonga_Defence_Services" class="mw-redirect" title="Tonga Defence Services">Tonga Defence Services</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The Tongan government supported the American "<a href="/wiki/Coalition_of_the_willing" title="Coalition of the willing">coalition of the willing</a>" action in <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a> and deployed 40+ soldiers (as part of an American force) in late 2004. The contingent returned home on 17 December 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> In 2007 a second contingent went to Iraq, and two more were sent during 2008 as part of continued support for the coalition. Tongan involvement concluded at the end of 2008 with no reported loss of life. </p>
      <p>In 2010, Brigadier General Tauʻaika ʻUtaʻatu, Commander of the <a href="/wiki/Tonga_Defence_Services" class="mw-redirect" title="Tonga Defence Services">Tonga Defence Services</a>, signed an agreement in London committing a minimum of 200 troops to co-operate with Britain's International Security Assistance Force (ISAF) in <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a>. The task completed in April 2014 and the UK presented Operational Service Medals to each of the soldiers involved during a parade held in Tonga.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Tonga has contributed troops and police to the <a href="/wiki/Bougainville_Province" class="mw-redirect" title="Bougainville Province">Bougainville</a> conflict in Papua-New Guinea and to the Australian-led <a href="/wiki/RAMSI" class="mw-redirect" title="RAMSI">RAMSI</a> force in the <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands" title="Solomon Islands">Solomon Islands</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tonga&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Tonga" title="Administrative divisions of Tonga">Administrative divisions of Tonga</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Tonga is sub-divided into five administrative divisions: <a href="/wiki/%CA%BBEua" title="ʻEua">ʻEua</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ha%CA%BBapai" title="Haʻapai">Haʻapai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Niuas" class="mw-redirect" title="Niuas">Niuas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tongatapu" title="Tongatapu">Tongatapu</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vava%CA%BBu" title="Vavaʻu">Vavaʻu</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tonga&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Tonga" title="Geography of Tonga">Geography of Tonga</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tonga_sm04.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Tonga_sm04.gif/220px-Tonga_sm04.gif" decoding="async" width="220" height="236" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Tonga_sm04.gif/330px-Tonga_sm04.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/9b/Tonga_sm04.gif 2x" data-file-width="364" data-file-height="391"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tonga_sm04.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A map of Tonga
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Located in <a href="/wiki/Oceania" title="Oceania">Oceania</a>, Tonga is an archipelago in the South <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a>, directly south of <a href="/wiki/Samoa" title="Samoa">Samoa</a> and about two-thirds of the way from <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a> to <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>. Its 169 islands, 36 of them inhabited,<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup> are divided into three main groups – <a href="/wiki/Vava%27u" class="mw-redirect" title="Vava'u">Vava'u</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ha%27apai" class="mw-redirect" title="Ha'apai">Ha'apai</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tongatapu" title="Tongatapu">Tongatapu</a> – and cover an 800-kilometre (500-mile)-long north–south line. </p>
      <p>The largest island, Tongatapu, on which the capital city of <a href="/wiki/Nuku%CA%BBalofa" title="Nukuʻalofa">Nukuʻalofa</a> is located, covers 257 square kilometres (99&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi). Geologically the Tongan islands are of two types: most have a limestone base formed from uplifted coral formations; others consist of limestone overlaying a <a href="/wiki/Volcanic" class="mw-redirect" title="Volcanic">volcanic</a> base. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tonga&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Tonga has a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_rainforest_climate" title="Tropical rainforest climate">tropical rainforest climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Af</a>) with a distinct warm period (December–April), during which the temperatures rise above 32&nbsp;°C (89.6&nbsp;°F), and a cooler period (May–November), with temperatures rarely rising above 27&nbsp;°C (80.6&nbsp;°F). The temperature and rainfall range from 23&nbsp;°C (73.4&nbsp;°F) and 1,700 millimetres (66.9 inches) on Tongatapu in the south to 27&nbsp;°C (80.6&nbsp;°F) and 2,970 millimetres (116.9 inches) on the more northerly islands closer to the Equator. The average wettest period is around March with on average 263&nbsp;mm (10.4&nbsp;in).<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> The average daily humidity is 80%. The highest temperature recorded in Tonga was 35&nbsp;°C (95&nbsp;°F) on 11 February 1979 in Vava'u. The coldest temperature recorded in Tonga was 8.7&nbsp;°C (47.7&nbsp;°F) on 8 September 1994 in Fua'amotu. Temperatures of 15&nbsp;°C (59&nbsp;°F) or lower are usually measured in the dry season and are more frequent in southern Tonga than in the north of the island.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> The tropical cyclone season currently runs from 1 November to 30 April, though tropical cyclones can form and affect Tonga outside of the season. </p>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ecology">Ecology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tonga&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Ecology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Tonga contains the <a href="/wiki/Tongan_tropical_moist_forests" title="Tongan tropical moist forests">Tongan tropical moist forests</a> terrestrial ecoregion.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-51">[51]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In Tonga, dating back to Tongan legend, flying bats are considered sacred and are the property of the monarchy. Thus they are protected and cannot be harmed or hunted. As a result, <a href="/wiki/Pteropus" title="Pteropus">flying fox bats</a> have thrived in many of the islands of Tonga.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/List_of_birds_of_Tonga" title="List of birds of Tonga">bird life of Tonga</a> include a total of 73 species, of which two are endemic; the <a href="/wiki/Tongan_Whistler" class="mw-redirect" title="Tongan Whistler">Tongan Whistler</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Tongan_megapode" title="Tongan megapode">Tongan megapode</a>. Five species have been introduced by humans, and eight are rare or accidental. Seven species are globally threatened. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tonga&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tongan_seniti_coin.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Tongan_seniti_coin.jpg/220px-Tongan_seniti_coin.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/ac/Tongan_seniti_coin.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="321" data-file-height="321"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tongan_seniti_coin.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A Tongan one-cent (<i>seniti taha</i>) coin
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Nuku_Island_Vava%27u.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Nuku_Island_Vava%27u.jpg/220px-Nuku_Island_Vava%27u.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Nuku_Island_Vava%27u.jpg/330px-Nuku_Island_Vava%27u.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Nuku_Island_Vava%27u.jpg/440px-Nuku_Island_Vava%27u.jpg 2x" data-file-width="584" data-file-height="375"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Nuku_Island_Vava%27u.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Nuku Island, <a href="/wiki/Vava%CA%BBu" title="Vavaʻu">Vavaʻu</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Majestic_Whale_Encounters8_-_pic_by_Brandon_Cole_(15799763491).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Majestic_Whale_Encounters8_-_pic_by_Brandon_Cole_%2815799763491%29.jpg/220px-Majestic_Whale_Encounters8_-_pic_by_Brandon_Cole_%2815799763491%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Majestic_Whale_Encounters8_-_pic_by_Brandon_Cole_%2815799763491%29.jpg/330px-Majestic_Whale_Encounters8_-_pic_by_Brandon_Cole_%2815799763491%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Majestic_Whale_Encounters8_-_pic_by_Brandon_Cole_%2815799763491%29.jpg/440px-Majestic_Whale_Encounters8_-_pic_by_Brandon_Cole_%2815799763491%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3189" data-file-height="2126"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Majestic_Whale_Encounters8_-_pic_by_Brandon_Cole_(15799763491).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Humpback_whale" title="Humpback whale">Humpback whales</a> of Tonga
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Tonga" title="Economy of Tonga">Economy of Tonga</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Tonga's economy is characterised by a large non-monetary sector and a heavy dependence on <a href="/wiki/Remittances" class="mw-redirect" title="Remittances">remittances</a> from the half of the country's population who live abroad (chiefly in Australia, New Zealand and the United States). The royal family and the nobles dominate and largely own the monetary sector of the economy – particularly the telecommunications and satellite services. Tonga was named the sixth most corrupt country in the world by Forbes magazine in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Tonga was ranked the 165th safest investment destination in the world in the March 2011 <a href="/wiki/Euromoney" title="Euromoney">Euromoney</a> Country Risk rankings.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The manufacturing sector consists of <a href="/wiki/Cottage_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Cottage industry">handicrafts</a> and a few other very small scale industries, which contribute only about 3% of GDP. Commercial business activities also are inconspicuous and, to a large extent, are dominated by the same large trading companies found throughout the South Pacific. In September 1974, the country's first commercial trading bank, the Bank of Tonga, opened. </p>
      <p>Tonga's development plans emphasise a growing private sector, upgrading agricultural productivity, revitalising the squash and vanilla bean industries, developing tourism, and improving communications and transport. Substantial progress has been made, but much work remains to be done. A small but growing construction sector is developing in response to the inflow of aid monies and remittances from Tongans abroad. In recognition of such a crucial contribution the present government has created a new department within the Prime Minister's Office with the sole purpose of catering for the needs of Tongans living abroad. Furthermore, in 2007 the Tongan Parliament amended citizenship laws to allow Tongans to hold dual citizenship.<sup id="cite_ref-b1_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-b1-56">[56]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><span class="anchor" id="Tourism"></span> The tourist industry is relatively undeveloped; however, the government recognises that tourism can play a major role in economic development, and efforts are being made to increase this source of revenue. Cruise ships often stop in <a href="/wiki/Vava%CA%BBu" title="Vavaʻu">Vavaʻu</a>, which has a reputation for its <a href="/wiki/Whale_watching" title="Whale watching">whale watching</a>, game fishing, surfing, beaches and is increasingly becoming a major player in the South Pacific tourism market.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Postage_stamps_and_postal_history_of_Tonga" title="Postage stamps and postal history of Tonga">Tonga's postage stamps</a>, which feature colourful and often unusual designs (including heart-shaped and banana-shaped stamps), are popular with <a href="/wiki/Philately" title="Philately">philatelists</a> around the world.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2005, the country became eligible to become a member of the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a>. After an initial voluntary delay, Tonga became a full member of the WTO on 27 July 2007. </p>
      <p>The Tonga Chamber of Commerce and Industry (TCCI), incorporated in 1996, endeavours to represent the interests of its members, private sector businesses, and to promote economic growth in the Kingdom. </p>
      <p>Tonga is home to some 106,000 people, but more than double that number live overseas, mainly in the US, New Zealand and Australia. Remittances from the overseas population have been declining since the onset of the 2008 global economic crisis. The tourism industry is improving, but remains modest at under 90,000 tourists per year.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture">Agriculture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tonga&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Agriculture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In Tonga, agriculture and forestry (together with fisheries) provide the majority of employment, foreign exchange earnings and food.<sup id="cite_ref-Halavatau_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Halavatau-60">[60]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Kunzel_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kunzel-61">[61]</a></sup> Rural Tongans rely on both <a href="/wiki/Plantation" title="Plantation">plantation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Subsistence_agriculture" title="Subsistence agriculture">subsistence agriculture</a>. Plants grown for both market <a href="/wiki/Cash_crop" title="Cash crop">cash crops</a> and home use include bananas, <a href="/wiki/Coconut" title="Coconut">coconuts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coffee_bean" title="Coffee bean">coffee beans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vanilla_bean" class="mw-redirect" title="Vanilla bean">vanilla beans</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Root_crops" class="mw-redirect" title="Root crops">root crops</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Cassava" title="Cassava">cassava</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sweet_potato" title="Sweet potato">sweet potato</a> and <a href="/wiki/Taro" title="Taro">taro</a>. As of 2001<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tonga&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, two-thirds of agricultural land was in root crops.<sup id="cite_ref-Halavatau_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Halavatau-60">[60]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The processing of coconuts into <a href="/wiki/Copra" title="Copra">copra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Desiccation" title="Desiccation">desiccated</a> (dried) coconut was once the only significant industry, and only commercial export, but deteriorating prices on the world market and lack of replanting brought this once vibrant industry, as in most island nations of the South Pacific, to a complete standstill. </p>
      <p>Pigs and poultry are the major types of livestock. Horses are kept for draft purposes, primarily by farmers working their ʻapi ʻuta (a plot of bushland). More cattle are being raised, and beef imports are declining.<sup id="cite_ref-b1_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-b1-56">[56]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The traditional feudal land ownership system meant that farmers had no incentive to invest in planting long-term tree crops on land they did not own, but in the late twentieth century kava and vanilla from larger plantations became the main agricultural exports, together with squash.<sup id="cite_ref-Halavatau_60-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Halavatau-60">[60]</a></sup> The export of squash to Japan, beginning in 1987, once brought relief to Tonga's struggling economy, but local farmers became increasingly wary of the Japanese market due to price fluctuations, not to mention the huge financial risks involved.<sup id="cite_ref-b1_56-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-b1-56">[56]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tonga&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Energy in Tonga mostly comes from imported diesel.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> Energy consumption in Tonga is projected to reach around 66 gigawatt hours by 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-64">[64]</a></sup> The country aims to reach 50% of renewable energy by 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-64">[64]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In view of the decreasing reliability of <a href="/wiki/Fossil-fuel_electricity" class="mw-redirect" title="Fossil-fuel electricity">fossil-fuel electricity</a> generation, its increasing costs and negative environmental side-effects, <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">renewable energy</a> solutions have attracted the government's attention. Together with <a href="/wiki/IRENA" class="mw-redirect" title="IRENA">IRENA</a>, Tonga has charted out a renewable energy based strategy to power the main and outer islands alike. The strategy focuses on solar home systems that turn individual households into small power plants. In addition, it calls for the involvement of local operators, finance institutions and technicians to provide sustainable business models as well as strategies to ensure the effective operation, management and maintenance once the systems are installed.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>With the assistance of IRENA, Tonga has developed the 2010–2020 Tonga Energy Road Map (TERM), which aims for a 50% reduction of diesel importation. This will be accomplished through a range of appropriate renewable technologies, including wind and solar, as well as innovative efficiencies.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2019, Tonga announced the construction of 6-megawatt solar farm on Tongatapu.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-67">[67]</a></sup> The plant will be the second largest solar plant in the Pacific upon completion.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-67">[67]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tonga&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tonga_demography.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Tonga_demography.png/220px-Tonga_demography.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="129" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Tonga_demography.png/330px-Tonga_demography.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Tonga_demography.png/440px-Tonga_demography.png 2x" data-file-width="724" data-file-height="426"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tonga_demography.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Tonga's population (1961–2003) in thousands
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Tonga" title="Demographics of Tonga">Demographics of Tonga</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Over 70% of the 103,197<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2019_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP_2019-10">[10]</a></sup> inhabitants live on its main island, <a href="/wiki/Tongatapu" title="Tongatapu">Tongatapu</a>. Although an increasing number of Tongans have moved into the only urban and commercial centre, Nukuʻalofa, where European and indigenous cultural and living patterns have blended, village life and kinship ties remain influential throughout the country. Despite emigration, Tonga grew in population from about 32,000 in the 1930s to more than 90,000 by 1976.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tonga&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Ethnic groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;">
