      </div> 
      <p>According to the government portal, Tongans, <a href="/wiki/Polynesians" title="Polynesians">Polynesian</a> by ethnicity with a mixture of <a href="/wiki/Melanesia" title="Melanesia">Melanesian</a>, represent more than 98% of the inhabitants. 1.5% are mixed Tongans and the rest are <a href="/wiki/European_ethnic_groups" class="mw-redirect" title="European ethnic groups">European</a> (the majority are British), mixed European, and other <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Islanders" class="mw-redirect" title="Pacific Islanders">Pacific Islanders</a>. In 2001 there were approximately 3,000 or 4,000 <a href="/wiki/Chinese_in_Tonga" title="Chinese in Tonga">Chinese in Tonga</a>, comprising 3 or 4% of the total Tongan population.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/2006_Nuku%CA%BBalofa_riots" title="2006 Nukuʻalofa riots">2006, Nukuʻalofa riots</a> mainly targeted Chinese-owned businesses, leading to the emigration of several hundred Chinese<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> so that only about 300 remain.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tonga&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Tongan_language" title="Tongan language">Tongan language</a> is the official language, along with English. Tongan, a <a href="/wiki/Polynesian_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Polynesian language">Polynesian language</a>, is closely related to <a href="/wiki/Wallisian_language" title="Wallisian language">Wallisian</a> (Uvean), <a href="/wiki/Niuean_language" title="Niuean language">Niuean</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hawaiian_language" title="Hawaiian language">Hawaiian</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Samoan_language" title="Samoan language">Samoan</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tonga&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Saione.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Saione.jpg/220px-Saione.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Saione.jpg/330px-Saione.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Saione.jpg/440px-Saione.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Saione.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Free_Wesleyan_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Free Wesleyan Church">Free Wesleyan Church</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Tonga does not have an official state religion.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> The Constitution of Tonga (Revised 1998) provides for freedom of religion.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1928, Queen <a href="/wiki/Salote_Tupou_III" class="mw-redirect" title="Salote Tupou III">Salote Tupou III</a>, who was a member of the <a href="/wiki/Free_Wesleyan_Church_of_Tonga" title="Free Wesleyan Church of Tonga">Free Wesleyan Church of Tonga</a>, established the Free Wesleyan Church as the state religion of Tonga. The chief pastor of the Free Wesleyan Church serves as the representative of the people of Tonga and of the Church at the coronation of a King or Queen of Tonga where he anoints and crowns the Monarch. In opposition to the establishment of the Free Wesleyan Church as a state religion, the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Tonga" title="Church of Tonga">Church of Tonga</a> separated from the Free Wesleyan Church in 1928. </p>
      <p>Everyday life is heavily influenced by Polynesian traditions and by the Christian faith; for example, all commerce and entertainment activities cease on Sunday, from the beginning of the day at midnight, to the end of the day at midnight. The constitution declares the Sabbath sacred forever. The official figures from the latest government census as of 2011<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tonga&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> show that 90% of the population are affiliated with a Christian church or sect, with the four major church affiliations in the kingdom as follows:<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Free_Wesleyan_Church_of_Tonga" title="Free Wesleyan Church of Tonga">Free Wesleyan Church of Tonga</a> (36,592 or 36%)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints</a> (18,554 or 18%)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_Tonga" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism in Tonga">Roman Catholics</a> (15,441 or 15%)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Free_Church_of_Tonga" title="Free Church of Tonga">Free Church of Tonga</a> (11,863 or 12%)</li>
      </ul> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints</a> sent missionaries in 1891 to visit King Siaosi (George) Tupo where they obtained permission to preach. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tonga&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>By some published surveys, Tonga has one of the highest obesity rates in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> data published in 2014 indicates that Tonga stands 4th overall in terms of <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Body_Mass_Index_(BMI)" class="mw-redirect" title="List of countries by Body Mass Index (BMI)">countries listed by mean body mass index data</a>. In 2011, 90% of the adult population were considered overweight using NIH interpretation of body mass index (BMI) data, with more than 60% of those <a href="/wiki/Obesity" title="Obesity">obese</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> 70% of Tongan females aged 15–85 are obese. Tonga and nearby <a href="/wiki/Nauru" title="Nauru">Nauru</a> have the world's highest overweight and obese populations.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tonga&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Tonga" title="Education in Tonga">Education in Tonga</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Primary education between ages 6 and 14 is compulsory and free in state schools. Mission schools provide about 8% of the primary and 90% of the secondary level of education. State schools make up for the rest. Higher education includes teacher training, nursing and medical training, a small private university, a woman's business college, and a number of private agricultural schools. Most higher education is pursued overseas. </p>
      <p>Tongans enjoy a relatively high level of education, with a 98.9% <a href="/wiki/Literacy" title="Literacy">literacy</a> rate,<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> and higher education up to and including medical and graduate degrees (pursued mostly overseas). They hold the body of academic knowledge created by their scholars in high esteem and the Kukū Kaunaka Collection which comprises every PhD and Masters dissertation written by any Tongan in any country is archived by <a href="/wiki/Seu%27ula_Johansson-Fua" title="Seu'ula Johansson-Fua">Seu'ula Johansson-Fua</a> at the Institute for Education in Tonga.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tonga&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Tonga" title="Culture of Tonga">Culture of Tonga</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Faikava.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Faikava.jpg/220px-Faikava.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Faikava.jpg/330px-Faikava.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Faikava.jpg/440px-Faikava.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1290" data-file-height="730"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Faikava.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Kava_culture" title="Kava culture">Kava culture</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Humans have lived in Tonga for nearly 3,000 years, since settlement in late <a href="/wiki/Lapita" class="mw-redirect" title="Lapita">Lapita</a> times. Before the arrival of European explorers in the late 17th and early 18th centuries, Tongans had frequent contacts with their nearest oceanic neighbours, <a href="/wiki/Fiji" title="Fiji">Fiji</a> and <a href="/wiki/Niue" title="Niue">Niue</a>. In the 19th century, with the arrival of Western traders and missionaries, Tongan culture changed, especially in religion. As of 2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tonga&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, almost 98&nbsp;percent of residents profess Christianity. The people discarded some old beliefs and habits and adopted others. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ula_fu.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Ula_fu.jpg/220px-Ula_fu.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/ba/Ula_fu.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="320" data-file-height="237"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Ula_fu.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The start of a Tongan <a href="/wiki/Tau%CA%BBolunga" title="Tauʻolunga">tauʻolunga</a> dance
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Contemporary Tongans often have strong ties to overseas lands. Many Tongans have emigrated to Australia, New Zealand, or the United States to seek employment and a higher standard of living. The United States is the preferred destination for Tongan emigrants, and as of 2000 there were 36,840 Tongans living in the US.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> More than 8,000 Tongans live in Australia.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> The Tongan <a href="/wiki/Diaspora" title="Diaspora">diaspora</a> retains close ties to relatives at home,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> and a significant portion of Tonga's income derives from remittances<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> to family members (often aged) who prefer to remain in Tonga. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tonga&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Tonga" title="Sport in Tonga">Sport in Tonga</a>
      </div> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Rugby">Rugby</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tonga&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Rugby">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">Rugby union</a> is the national sport,<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Tonga_national_rugby_union_team" title="Tonga national rugby union team">national team</a> (ʻIkale Tahi, or Sea Eagles) has performed quite well on the international stage. Tonga has competed in six <a href="/wiki/Rugby_World_Cup" title="Rugby World Cup">Rugby World Cups</a> since <a href="/wiki/1987_Rugby_World_Cup" title="1987 Rugby World Cup">1987</a>. The <a href="/wiki/2007_Rugby_World_Cup" title="2007 Rugby World Cup">2007</a> and <a href="/wiki/2011_Rugby_World_Cup" title="2011 Rugby World Cup">2011 Rugby World Cups</a> were Tonga's most successful to date, both winning two out of four matches and in a running chance for the quarter finals. In the <a href="/wiki/2007_Rugby_World_Cup" title="2007 Rugby World Cup">2007 Rugby World Cup</a>, Tonga won its first two matches, against the <a href="/wiki/United_States_national_rugby_union_team" title="United States national rugby union team">USA</a> 25–15, and <a href="/wiki/Samoa_national_rugby_union_team" title="Samoa national rugby union team">Samoa</a> 19–15. They came very close to upsetting the eventual winners of the 2007 tournament, the South African <a href="/wiki/Springboks" class="mw-redirect" title="Springboks">Springboks</a>, losing 30–25. A defeat by <a href="/wiki/England_National_Rugby_Union_Team" class="mw-redirect" title="England National Rugby Union Team">England</a>, 36–20 in their last pool game ended their hopes of making the knockout stages. Nevertheless, by picking up third place in their pool games behind South Africa and England, Tonga earned automatic qualification for the 2011 Rugby World Cup in New Zealand. In <a href="/wiki/2011_Rugby_World_Cup_Pool_A" title="2011 Rugby World Cup Pool A">Pool A</a> of the <a href="/wiki/2011_Rugby_World_Cup" title="2011 Rugby World Cup">2011 Rugby World Cup</a>, Tonga beat both <a href="/wiki/Japan_national_rugby_union_team" title="Japan national rugby union team">Japan</a> 31–18 and 5th ranked<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> eventual finalist <a href="/wiki/France_national_rugby_union_team" title="France national rugby union team">France</a> 19–14 in the latter pool stages. However, a previous heavy defeat by the <a href="/wiki/All_Blacks" class="mw-redirect" title="All Blacks">All Blacks</a> at the tournament's opener (41–10) and a subsequent tight defeat by <a href="/wiki/Canada_national_rugby_union_team" title="Canada national rugby union team">Canada</a> (25–20) meant that Tonga lost out to France (who also lost to <a href="/wiki/All_Blacks" class="mw-redirect" title="All Blacks">NZ</a>) for the quarter finals due to 2 bonus points and a points difference of 46. </p>
      <p>Tonga's best result before 2007 came in <a href="/wiki/1995_Rugby_World_Cup" title="1995 Rugby World Cup">1995</a>, when they beat <a href="/wiki/Ivory_Coast_national_rugby_union_team" title="Ivory Coast national rugby union team">Côte d'Ivoire</a> 29–11, and <a href="/wiki/1999_Rugby_World_Cup" title="1999 Rugby World Cup">1999</a> when they beat Italy 28–25 (although with only 14 men they lost heavily to England, 101–10). Tonga perform the <a href="/wiki/Kailao" title="Kailao">Ikale Tahi war dance</a> or Sipi Tau (a form of <a href="/wiki/Kailao" title="Kailao">Kailao</a>) before all their matches. Tonga used to compete in the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Tri-Nations" title="Pacific Tri-Nations">Pacific Tri-Nations</a> against Samoa and Fiji, which has now been replaced by the <a href="/wiki/IRB_Pacific_Nations_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="IRB Pacific Nations Cup">IRB Pacific Nations Cup</a>, which now involves <a href="/wiki/Japan_national_rugby_union_team" title="Japan national rugby union team">Japan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canada_national_rugby_union_team" title="Canada national rugby union team">Canada</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_national_rugby_union_team" title="United States national rugby union team">United States</a>. At club level, there are the <a href="/wiki/Datec_Cup_Provincial_Championship" title="Datec Cup Provincial Championship">Datec Cup Provincial Championship</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Rugby_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="Pacific Rugby Cup">Pacific Rugby Cup</a>. Rugby union is governed by the <a href="/wiki/Tonga_Rugby_Football_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Tonga Rugby Football Union">Tonga Rugby Football Union</a>, which was a member of the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Islands_Rugby_Alliance" title="Pacific Islands Rugby Alliance">Pacific Islands Rugby Alliance</a> and contributed to the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Islanders_rugby_union_team" title="Pacific Islanders rugby union team">Pacific Islanders rugby union team</a>, before they were disbanded in 2009. </p>
      <p>Many players of Tongan descent – e.g., <a href="/wiki/Jonah_Lomu" title="Jonah Lomu">Jonah Lomu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Israel_Folau" title="Israel Folau">Israel Folau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Viliami_Ofahengaue" title="Viliami Ofahengaue">Viliami "William" ʻOfahengaue</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malakai_Fekitoa" title="Malakai Fekitoa">Malakai Fekitoa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ben_Afeaki" title="Ben Afeaki">Ben Afeaki</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Piutau" title="Charles Piutau">Charles Piutau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frank_Halai" title="Frank Halai">Frank Halai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sekope_Kepu" title="Sekope Kepu">Sekope Kepu</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Smith_(rugby_union)" title="George Smith (rugby union)">George Smith</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cliff_Palu" class="mw-redirect" title="Cliff Palu">Wycliff Palu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sitaleki_Timani" title="Sitaleki Timani">Sitaleki Timani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salesi_Ma%27afu" title="Salesi Ma'afu">Salesi Ma'afu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Faingaa" class="mw-redirect" title="Anthony Faingaa">Anthony</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saia_Faingaa" class="mw-redirect" title="Saia Faingaa">Saia Faingaa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mark_Gerrard" title="Mark Gerrard">Mark Gerrard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cooper_Vuna" title="Cooper Vuna">Cooper Vuna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Doug_Howlett" title="Doug Howlett">Doug Howlett</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toutai_Kefu" title="Toutai Kefu">Toutai Kefu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tatafu_Polota-Nau" title="Tatafu Polota-Nau">Tatafu Polota-Nau</a> – have played for either the All Blacks or the Wallabies. <a href="/wiki/British_and_Irish_Lions" title="British and Irish Lions">British and Irish Lion</a> and Welsh international player <a href="/wiki/Taulupe_Faletau" title="Taulupe Faletau">Taulupe "Toby" Faletau</a> is Tongan born and the son of Tongan international <a href="/wiki/Kuli_Faletau" title="Kuli Faletau">Kuli Faletau</a>. Taulupe's cousins and England international players <a href="/wiki/Billy_Vunipola" title="Billy Vunipola">Billy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mako_Vunipola" title="Mako Vunipola">Mako Vunipola</a> (who is also a <a href="/wiki/British_and_Irish_Lion" class="mw-redirect" title="British and Irish Lion">British and Irish Lion</a>), are sons of former Tonga rugby captain <a href="/wiki/Fe%27ao_Vunipola" class="mw-redirect" title="Fe'ao Vunipola">Fe'ao Vunipola</a>. Rugby is popular among the nation's schools, and students from schools such as Tonga College and <a href="/wiki/Tupou_College" title="Tupou College">Tupou College</a> are regularly offered scholarships in New Zealand, Australia and Japan. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Rugby_league" title="Rugby league">Rugby league</a> has gained some success. Tonga made their first appearance at a <a href="/wiki/Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="Rugby League World Cup">Rugby League World Cup</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1995_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="1995 Rugby League World Cup">1995</a> edition where they went out in the first stage but narrowly lost to <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_national_rugby_league_team" title="New Zealand national rugby league team">New Zealand</a>. They have since appeared in each subsequent Rugby League World Cup tournament. In the <a href="/wiki/2008_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="2008 Rugby League World Cup">2008 Rugby League World Cup</a> <a href="/wiki/Tonga_national_rugby_league_team" title="Tonga national rugby league team">Tonga</a> recorded wins against <a href="/wiki/Ireland_national_rugby_league_team" title="Ireland national rugby league team">Ireland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scotland_national_rugby_league_team" title="Scotland national rugby league team">Scotland</a>. Just before the <a href="/wiki/2017_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="2017 Rugby League World Cup">2017 World Cup</a>, various high-profile players, led by <a href="/wiki/Jason_Taumalolo" title="Jason Taumalolo">Jason Taumalolo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Fifita" title="Andrew Fifita">Andrew Fifita</a>, defected from their tier one nations to represent their nation of heritage. This led to them defeating New Zealand in Hamilton at <a href="/wiki/Waikato_Stadium" title="Waikato Stadium">Waikato Stadium</a> on 11 November at that tournament. The national team has since also recorded victories again <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain_national_rugby_league_team" title="Great Britain national rugby league team">Great Britain</a> and the world number one <a href="/wiki/Australia_national_rugby_league_team" title="Australia national rugby league team">Australia</a>. In addition to the success of the national team, many players of Tongan descent make it big in the Australian <a href="/wiki/National_Rugby_League" title="National Rugby League">National Rugby League</a> competition. These include <a href="/wiki/Jason_Taumalolo" title="Jason Taumalolo">Jason Taumalolo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Israel_Folau" title="Israel Folau">Israel Folau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tyson_Frizell" title="Tyson Frizell">Tyson Frizell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tevita_Pangai_Junior" title="Tevita Pangai Junior">Tevita Pangai Junior</a>, <a href="/wiki/Konrad_Hurrell" title="Konrad Hurrell">Konrad Hurrell</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Fusitua" class="mw-redirect" title="David Fusitua">David Fusitua</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tuimoala_Lolohea" title="Tuimoala Lolohea">Tuimoala Lolohea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sio_Siua_Taukeiaho" title="Sio Siua Taukeiaho">Sio Siua Taukeiaho</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Taufua" title="Jorge Taufua">Jorge Taufua</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_Hopoate" title="William Hopoate">William Hopoate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Fifita" title="Andrew Fifita">Andrew Fifita</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ben_Murdoch-Masila" title="Ben Murdoch-Masila">Ben Murdoch-Masila</a>, <a href="/wiki/Felise_Kaufusi" title="Felise Kaufusi">Felise Kaufusi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Willie_Mason" title="Willie Mason">Willie Mason</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manu_Vatuvei" title="Manu Vatuvei">Manu Vatuvei</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brent_Kite" title="Brent Kite">Brent Kite</a>, <a href="/wiki/Willie_Tonga" title="Willie Tonga">Willie Tonga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Tupou" title="Anthony Tupou">Anthony Tupou</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Kaufusi" title="Antonio Kaufusi">Antonio Kaufusi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jennings_(rugby_league)" title="Michael Jennings (rugby league)">Michael Jennings</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tony_Williams_(rugby_league)" title="Tony Williams (rugby league)">Tony Williams</a>, <a href="/wiki/Feleti_Mateo" title="Feleti Mateo">Feleti Mateo</a> to name a few... Subsequently, some Tongan rugby league players have established successful careers in the <a href="/wiki/Super_League" title="Super League">Super League</a> such as Antonio Kaufusi.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Olympics">Olympics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tonga&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Olympics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tonga_at_the_Olympics" title="Tonga at the Olympics">Tonga at the Olympics</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Aside from rugby, Tonga has also produced athletes who have competed at both the Summer and Winter Olympics. Tonga's only Olympic medal came from the <a href="/wiki/1996_Summer_Olympics" title="1996 Summer Olympics">1996 Summer Olympics</a> in Atlanta, where <a href="/wiki/Paea_Wolfgramm" title="Paea Wolfgramm">Paea Wolfgramm</a> won silver in <a href="/wiki/Boxing_at_the_1996_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Super_heavyweight" title="Boxing at the 1996 Summer Olympics – Super heavyweight">super heavyweight</a> boxing. One athlete attended the <a href="/wiki/2018_Winter_Olympics" title="2018 Winter Olympics">2018 Winter Olympics</a> in Pyeongchang, South Korea. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="American_football">American football</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tonga&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: American football">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>Several Tongans have been football players in the <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">National Football League</a> (NFL), including <a href="/wiki/Tuineau_Alipate" title="Tuineau Alipate">Tuineau Alipate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spencer_Folau" title="Spencer Folau">Spencer Folau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lakei_Heimuli" title="Lakei Heimuli">Lakei Heimuli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Steve_Kaufusi" title="Steve Kaufusi">Steve Kaufusi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ma%27ake_Kemoeatu" class="mw-redirect" title="Ma'ake Kemoeatu">Ma'ake Kemoeatu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deuce_Lutui" title="Deuce Lutui">Deuce Lutui</a>, <a href="/wiki/Siupeli_Malamala" title="Siupeli Malamala">Siupeli Malamala</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tim_Manoa" title="Tim Manoa">Tim Manoa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stan_Mataele" title="Stan Mataele">Stan Mataele</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vili_Maumau" title="Vili Maumau">Vili Maumau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Pupunu" title="Alfred Pupunu">Alfred Pupunu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vai_Sikahema" title="Vai Sikahema">Vai Sikahema</a>, <a href="/wiki/Star_Lotulelei" title="Star Lotulelei">Star Lotulelei</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Peter_Tuipulotu" title="Peter Tuipulotu">Peter Tuipulotu</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tonga&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tonga&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

        <li><i>The Art of Tonga</i> (Ko e ngaahi'aati'o Tonga) by Keith St Cartmail. (1997) Honolulu&nbsp;: University of Hawai`i Press.

        <li><i>The Tonga Book</i> by Paul. W. Dale</li> 
        <li><i>Tonga</i> by James Siers</li>
       </ul>
